  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ebd9a0e4-55f5-4f24-a929-e797beada815'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8004366339535499391">It's a night like any other on board the Icarus. Then, catastrophe strikes: the massive luxury spaceliner is yanked out of hyperspace and plummets into the nearest planet. Lilac LaRoux and Tarver Merendsen survive. And they seem to be alone. <br/><br/>Lilac is the daughter of the richest man in the universe. Tarver comes from nothing, a young war hero who learned long ago that girls</span>
  <span id="freeText8004366339535499391" style="display:none">It's a night like any other on board the Icarus. Then, catastrophe strikes: the massive luxury spaceliner is yanked out of hyperspace and plummets into the nearest planet. Lilac LaRoux and Tarver Merendsen survive. And they seem to be alone. <br /><br />Lilac is the daughter of the richest man in the universe. Tarver comes from nothing, a young war hero who learned long ago that girls like Lilac are more trouble than they’re worth. But with only each other to rely on, Lilac and Tarver must work together, making a tortuous journey across the eerie, deserted terrain to seek help. <br /><br />Then, against all odds, Lilac and Tarver find a strange blessing in the tragedy that has thrown them into each other’s arms. Without the hope of a future together in their own world, they begin to wonder—would they be better off staying here forever?<br /><br />Everything changes when they uncover the truth behind the chilling whispers that haunt their every step. Lilac and Tarver may find a way off this planet. But they won’t be the same people who landed on it.<br /><br />The Starbound Trilogy: Three worlds. Three love stories. One enemy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8004366339535499391" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/399494-firstly-i-d-like-to-say-that-this-book">Firstly, I&#39;d like to say that this book looks fantastic. However, there&#39;s something that I&#39;ve noticed here and in other stories that needs to be brought up. The spaceship that crashes is called the Icarus. DON&#39;T NAME YOUR SPACESHIP AFTER ICARUS! It&#39;s gonna crash! What kind of idiot names their flying thing after someone famous for trying to fly, doing something stupid, falling out of the sky and DYING?</a>
</div>

<div id="review_793675027" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/793675027" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/793675027?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer793675027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer523994767035015471">I am crazy minority lady :(<br/><br/>Let me break down my thought process on this book from the very first time I noticed it on goodreads because somewhere along the way something went really really wrong. Just a quick scroll down the GR page and I can see all my friends' ratings of five or four stars... but the attraction is lost on me.<br/><br/><b>1) The description appears on goodreads.</b> We are promised science fiction and space and "a tortuous journey across the eerie, deserted terrain". A setting in space, a story</span>
  <span id="freeText523994767035015471" style="display:none">I am crazy minority lady :(<br><br>Let me break down my thought process on this book from the very first time I noticed it on goodreads because somewhere along the way something went really really wrong. Just a quick scroll down the GR page and I can see all my friends' ratings of five or four stars... but the attraction is lost on me.<br><br><b>1) The description appears on goodreads.</b> We are promised science fiction and space and "a tortuous journey across the eerie, deserted terrain". A setting in space, a story of survival and a couple of horny teenagers? Sounds like it could be a wild ride. I don't know about you but I love space stories and the vast arena of possibility which they open. I've enjoyed everything from Revis's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8235178.Across_the_Universe__Across_the_Universe___1_" title="Across the Universe (Across the Universe, #1) by Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Universe</a> series to Clarke's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/70535.2001_A_Space_Odyssey__Space_Odyssey___1_" title="2001 A Space Odyssey (Space Odyssey, #1) by Arthur C. Clarke" rel="nofollow noopener">2001: A Space Odyssey</a>. Because anything could happen. There's an extra layer of possibility to the fantasy that makes you wonder if it could be true because there are so many unexplored corners where our science fiction tales could very well be fact.<br><br><b>2) The cover reveal.</b> Uh oh. And there it is. Not that I don't like the cover, I love myself some glitter and pretty dresses as much as the next magpie, but you can probably guess why my hopes started to crumble. I remember the first hardback edition of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11809168.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a>. Do you?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1310676610l/11809168.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>I'm dystopian, I swear! I'm big, I'm bad and... shit, I think I broke a nail.</b>
</i> I remember how I told myself it would be fine. I mean, the description was promising hardcore dystopian fiction! It wouldn't lie to me, would it? Weeellll... <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/240209169" rel="nofollow noopener">I wrote a review about that</a>.<br><br><b>3) The reviews start rolling in.</b> It seems as though I was very wrong to judge this book by its cover. Reviews from some of my most trusty friends appeared and they LOVED this book. Is it even possible? Could I be completely wrong? I mean, Beth Revis's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8235178.Across_the_Universe__Across_the_Universe___1_" title="Across the Universe (Across the Universe, #1) by Beth Revis" rel="nofollow noopener">Across the Universe</a> was all pink and twinkly and romance-like and I enjoyed that book. I must read it to find out!<br><br><b>4) I think I read the wrong book.</b> I think we all know those moments when we've heard so many great things about a book and we pick up said book only to discover that the magic hasn't touched us. But I was really disappointed with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13138635.These_Broken_Stars__Starbound___1_" title="These Broken Stars (Starbound, #1) by Amie Kaufman" rel="nofollow noopener">These Broken Stars</a> and should have listened to my instincts when I saw the pretty cover.<br><br>Most of the actual space action in this book happens in the first couple of chapters. After the two main characters - Lilac and Tarver - crash land on a planet, it becomes a long-winded trek through a jungle-like setting. I was disappointed to say goodbye to the sky and stars so soon but would have easily forgiven the book if I'd enjoyed the survival part of the story which followed. But, honestly, I found it painfully slow and boring. And all orchestrated around the romance.<br><br>This book is predominantly a romance. Description aside, survival/space parts aside, this book is about getting Lilac and Tarver together. Which may be exactly what you want. If you like your romance heavy and your action on the side, then pick this up. But it's not really my thing. And I got a distinct sense that everything in this book was built around the romantic aspect. Each scene felt deliberate in a way that would put the characters in such a situation that Tarver would have to save Lilac or they would have to remove their clothing or sleep huddled together. The action never felt real, it felt like a series of flirtations between the two teens. Finding new clothes is an excuse for Tarver to admire Lilac's body. A chilly night is an excuse for Tarver to sleep with his erection pressed against her ass.<br><br>But I think the most disappointing thing of all is the sheer lack of world-building. The setting of this novel is enormous and holds huge and fabulous opportunity - we're in a whole new part of the universe! And yet, there is almost zero world-building. I feel like I know nothing about the society that Lilac and Tarver come from. I appreciate that this is going to be a trilogy but, hell, give me something!<br><br>I think it's fair to say that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13138635.These_Broken_Stars__Starbound___1_" title="These Broken Stars (Starbound, #1) by Amie Kaufman" rel="nofollow noopener">These Broken Stars</a> wasn't the book for me. Maybe I'll learn to follow my initial instincts about those jazzy covers in future.</span>
  <a data-text-id="523994767035015471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_262679778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/262679778" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/262679778?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-publication">2013-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=sci-fi-or-futuristic">sci-fi-or-futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=crush-worthy-boys">crush-worthy-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=aussies">aussies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=heroines-butt-kicking">heroines-butt-kicking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=own-dtb-tbr">own-dtb-tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=december">december</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer262679778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12933524267214375332"><b>4.5 stars</b> Here's what you need to know:<br/><br/>-- This story is incredibly original, and unlike any other scifi book I've ever read before. Leaps and bounds above most YA science fiction for sure, and with an interesting mood/tone that you don't often find in this genre.<br/><br/>-- Much of the book is also a survival story, so if you like that sort of thing (as I do!), this one will probably interest you.<br/><br/>-- The writing is terrific. Don't let the "Titanic in space" idea fool you; while technically true (and a spe</span>
  <span id="freeText12933524267214375332" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b> Here's what you need to know:<br /><br />-- This story is incredibly original, and unlike any other scifi book I've ever read before. Leaps and bounds above most YA science fiction for sure, and with an interesting mood/tone that you don't often find in this genre.<br /><br />-- Much of the book is also a survival story, so if you like that sort of thing (as I do!), this one will probably interest you.<br /><br />-- The writing is terrific. Don't let the "Titanic in space" idea fool you; while technically true (and a spectacular crash indeed), there's much more complexity to this story than that. <br /><br />-- The two main characters are fantastic, both as individuals and together.<br /><br />-- Serious swoon, guys. Serious swoon.<br /><br />-- Recommended for fans of Andrea Host's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10837174.Stray__Touchstone___1_" title="Stray (Touchstone, #1) by Andrea K. Höst" rel="nofollow noopener">Stray</a>, possibly Sangu Mandanna's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13062488.The_Lost_Girl" title="The Lost Girl by Sangu Mandanna" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Girl</a>, possibly Alison Goodman's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/462225.Singing_the_Dogstar_Blues" title="Singing the Dogstar Blues by Alison Goodman" rel="nofollow noopener">Singing the Dogstar Blues</a>, and definitely fans of Star Trek: The Next Generation.<br /><br />The authors shared the story of how that gorgeous title came to be. Fun fact: it was almost called MASSIVE CRASH. :D <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/02/tbscoverreveal.html">www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/02/tbs...</a><br /><br /><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for this mini review.</i></span>

<div id="review_789304247" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/789304247" />
    <a title="Navessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa"><img alt="Navessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1444162983p2/18104163.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/789304247?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navessa" href="/user/show/18104163-navessa">Navessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

Five stars.</b><br/><br/>You know why? Because I enjoyed the <i>shit</i> out of this book. <br/><br/>You want a detailed breakdown of what happens in it? <br/><br/>Look elsewhere. <br/><br/>You want me to tell you how fucking gloriously understated yet wholly satisfying this world building was? <br/><br/>Too bad. <br/><br/>You want to know why I started losing my mind 70% in? <br/><br/>HOW'S IT FEEL TO WANT? <br/><br/>This book is everything that makes me keep coming back to the YA category.   <span id="freeText17586531364968480120" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420147458i/13181559.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Boom. Because I enjoyed the <i>shit</i> out of this book. <br><br>You want a detailed breakdown of what happens in it? <br><br>Look elsewhere. <br><br>You want me to tell you how fucking gloriously understated yet wholly satisfying this world building was? <br><br>Too bad. <br><br>You want to know why I started losing my mind 70% in? <br><br>HOW'S IT FEEL TO WANT? <br><br>This book is everything that makes me keep coming back to the YA category. This book was a not only refreshingly original, but filled with all sorts of delicious mind-fuckery. <br><br>*applause*<br><br><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer18344994381922000266">at first, this story was giving me major ‘titanic in space’ vibes. and then it became like ‘castaway in space.’ and im not mad about any of it.<br/><br/>i thought the story was fun. the sci-fi aspect isnt the strongest (if youre comparing it to other books in the genre), but the world is cool and the characters are worth reading about. <br/><br/>i will say though, at the end, i did ask myself ‘what was even the point of this?’ im hoping this will be answered in the next book because the story definitely feels unres</span>
  <span id="freeText18344994381922000266" style="display:none">at first, this story was giving me major ‘titanic in space’ vibes. and then it became like ‘castaway in space.’ and im not mad about any of it.<br /><br />i thought the story was fun. the sci-fi aspect isnt the strongest (if youre comparing it to other books in the genre), but the world is cool and the characters are worth reading about. <br /><br />i will say though, at the end, i did ask myself ‘what was even the point of this?’ im hoping this will be answered in the next book because the story definitely feels unresolved on its own.<br /><br />but overall, i definitely enjoyed this more than i thought i would!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_619972874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/619972874" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/619972874?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=awesome-guy">awesome-guy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer619972874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13748479423116320078"><blockquote>
  <i>This is a wilderness waiting to swallow me; I’d barely make a dent trying to fight it. There are no rules for me to learn, no points to be scored, no bluffs to be called. This is a hell I’ve never imagined.<br/>And I think I’m going to die here.</i>
</blockquote>A lot of people have been calling this an intergalactic <i>Titanic</i>, and while there are certain similarities, particularly in the beginning of the book, the parallels to that doomed cruise liner ends there. I really liked this book. This is a beautifully writ</span>
  <span id="freeText13748479423116320078" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>This is a wilderness waiting to swallow me; I’d barely make a dent trying to fight it. There are no rules for me to learn, no points to be scored, no bluffs to be called. This is a hell I’ve never imagined.<br />And I think I’m going to die here.</i>
</blockquote>A lot of people have been calling this an intergalactic <i>Titanic</i>, and while there are certain similarities, particularly in the beginning of the book, the parallels to that doomed cruise liner ends there. I really liked this book. This is a beautifully written space opera, with elements of the paranormal. The plot is very much survival-based, and more than anything, it is the relationship between the survivors that makes this book stand out.<br /><br />The writing is beautiful, the descriptions are exceptionally well done, without any elements of purple prose; it flowed exceedingly well, and had I not known that this was a collaboration between two authors, I never would have suspected that this book was co-authored. The romance was well built, and completely believable, although a little overwhelming at times given the environment and the situation. I wound up liking both of the characters, even if I didn't start off that way. Lilac and Tarver's relationship and its development was the best thing about this book. <b>Warning: I wanted to punch Lilac in the face for the first 30% of the novel. She improves, I promise.</b><br /><br />With that said, I do have reservations about the book that keeps it from being a great novel, including <b>the slowness of the plot, the unconvincing character of Tarver (however much I love him, and I do love him), and the complete lack of world building</b>.<br /><br />The plot dragged on at times because an overwhelming part of the book is composed of the pair traipsing through an alien planet, trying to survive an unknown environment. The narrative flows well, but Tarver's character does not seem convincing to me as a male. He feels a lot like Ethan Wates, in the Beautiful Creatures series, for the femininity of his narration. He is a soldier, he is toughness mixed with compassion, but there are certain aspects about his narrative that does not make him feel entirely realistic as an 18-year old boy.<br /><br /><u>The Summary</u>: Lilac LaRoux is the wealthiest heiress in the galaxy. She has spent her life surrounded by adoring fans, false friends, due to her status as the adored daughter of the galaxy's wealthiest man, a self-made engineer. He is a loving father who suffocates Lilac with his ovoerprotectiveness. Lilac knows that her father is only too willing to destroy any man who dares to come close to his precious only daughter.<blockquote>
  <i>Lilac Rose LaRoux. Untouchable. Toxic.<br />I should’ve been named Ivy, or Foxglove, or Belladonna.</i>
</blockquote>Tarver Merendsen is 18, a war hero, more due to luck than anything. Heavily decorated for a brave act, he is now an honored guest on board the spaceship <i>Icarus</i>, but feels largely like a monkey being paraded around, until one beautiful red-headed girl catches his eyes. Lilac has no choice. She rejects him coldly. Humiliates him in front of a crowd. Lilac knows the consequences if her father finds out that this lower-class young man is interested in his princess.<br /><br />Despite their distrust of one another, Lilac and Tarver are thrown together in an escape pod when something goes terribly wrong. Something has knocked the <i>Icarus</i> out of hyperspace. The ship is going to be destroyed.<blockquote>
  <i>A ripple of white-hot energy shoots through its metal frame. I taste copper, and then the universe goes black with a sound like a thunderclap in my ears. All the lights, the countdown, even the emergency lighting … gone. We’re left in utter blackness but for the stars outside the viewport.<br />Stars that are no longer stretched thin. The Icarus has been torn out of hyperspace.</i>
</blockquote>The passengers must evacuate in the life pods. The Titanic had over 1100 people on board. The Icarus has over 50,000 passengers, and few survivors.<br /><br />Their escape pod lands on an alien planet. The air seems safe to breathe, but the environment is nothing like what Lilac has known before. Lilac has grown up in a simulated natural environment, with perfect trees, perfect landscapes, she is unused to the reality of real, unsimulated terrain and its dangers, but she is tougher than she looks. Tarver, as a military man, is much more in command of the situation. <br /><br />Lilac and Tarver have to work together. She is terrified, afraid, but brave, masking her insecurities with anger and hatred. He is still biting from the humiliation he received on board the ship, angry, frustrated at his attraction to her, despite her attitude. The two have a lot to work through if they are to remain alive long enough to be rescued.<br /><br />But survival is not all they have to be concerned about. There is something strange going on on this alien planet. There are glimpses of things, shadows of people, disembodied voices. Is it the hallucinations of two minds in shock, or is it something more?<br /><br /><u>The Premise</u>: One of my sole complaints in the book. Frankly, there is none. It's like being plunged into the middle of a season of Star Trek. Sure, it's entertaining, but man, give us some effing background, would ya? There is absolutely nothing about the past, about the present. There's not much mention of technology besides the hyperspace drive and escape pods and stars and a sci-fi-ish gun. There is nothing about the culture, the history. We don't know why this society is so strictly class-segregated. <b>We know absolutely jack shit about this setting. It is a futuristic novel in name only.</b><br /><br /><u>The Characters</u>: Loved them. I didn't expect this, because, as I mentioned, I spent about 30% of the book wanting to punch Lilac in the face, but Lilac turns out to be just the type of female character I like. <b>Lilac is initially imperfect, even abonimable at points, but she matures from the experience; she has character, she is never one-dimensional</b>. Lilac is a spoiled, pampered princess, but she is smart. However, what made me hate her at first was her attitude of <b>"I must be strong: strong means bitchy."</b> She is an absolute terror to poor Tarver in the beginning, as he struggles to get both of them to safety, and she persists on being obnoxious for a large chunk of the novel, in order to feel like she has control of the situation.<blockquote>
  <i>His opinion of me is already a lost cause—years later, when he looks back at this escapade, I’d rather he think bitch, than weakling.</i>
</blockquote>Lila starts off being overly stubborn to the point of hurting herself. She is so determined to prove herself strong, right in everything she does that she will not admit to being wrong. Lilac would trample through a forest wearing high heels and a ball gown, for the sake of her pride. In her defense, and I like this about her, she does not complain. She ends up shredding her feet to shreds, and she does not shed a tear. Her pride will only go so far, and Lilac becomes a much more likeable character once she gets over herself. She is not afraid to admit she is wrong.<blockquote>
  <i>So yes, I was cruel afterward. I’m cruel because it’s the fastest way to get a man to lose interest, and trust me, I’ve learned how. My father taught me well. And maybe I’m cruel because it’s easy, and because it’s something...something I can be good at.</i>
</blockquote>I really like Tarver's character, he is an absolute gentleman, and if I were to be stranded on a desert island, I'd want him as my partner. <b>However, Tarver's narration does not feel accurate as an actual teenaged male to me.</b> Yes, he is a soldier, but he is overwhelmingly, exceedingly romantic in his perception of Lilac from the very beginning, and as much as I like him, he is unconvincing as a <b>man</b>. He is too effeminate. For example, these are some of his observations about Lilac:<br /><br /><i>"Both her eyes are marked underneath with dark smears of blue and purple, and one is still marbled black and yellow as her magnificent black eye starts to fade. She’s pale, with new freckles from the sun overhead standing out like punctuation on a page.<br />But she’s captivating too, maybe more than she was before."<br /><br />"There are dirty smudges mingling with the freckles all over her face, and that bruise on her cheek. Even in sleep, her mouth is pulled into a straight, determined line.<br />There are purple half circles underneath her eyes, and she’s sweaty, beat up, and utterly exhausted.<br />She’s never looked so beautiful."</i><br /><br />Tarver's part of the narration is littered with his feelings, how much he finds Lilac beautiful, lovely, captivating. <b>He constantly makes observations on her beauty, her hair, the marks on her face, the ways she enchants him. Tarver is an awesome guy, but he's just not a realistic one.</b><br /><br /><u>The Romance</u>: I loved the way the romance between Lilac and Tarver was portrayed in this book. They start out as enemies, and their feelings grew beyond that, into trust, friendship, and something more. It was a really well-written love story. I love seeing from both their narratives, how their feelings and internal conflicts grew and changed, how they got past their reservations, how they gradually fell in love. Sweet is the best word to describe their romance.<br /><br />Overall, a well-written and interesting novel that is quite different from most YA paranormals and sci-fi out there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13748479423116320078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1310840983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10695685715780459899">I really enjoyed this book the second time around! <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492371328i/22510652.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The first time I read this book was back in 2015 and I'm not sure why I gave it 2.5 stars. I had an old review that told me some of the reasons but they make no sense to me now! <br/><br/>I loved Tarver and Lilac and yes I wanted to smack them a few times. I always feel like that so it's nothing new. <br/><br/>Lilac is the daughter of one of the richest men if not the richest men and Tarver is a lowly Major that didn't come from a whole lot. They didn't really like</span>
  <span id="freeText10695685715780459899" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book the second time around! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492371328i/22510652.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first time I read this book was back in 2015 and I'm not sure why I gave it 2.5 stars. I had an old review that told me some of the reasons but they make no sense to me now! <br><br>I loved Tarver and Lilac and yes I wanted to smack them a few times. I always feel like that so it's nothing new. <br><br>Lilac is the daughter of one of the richest men if not the richest men and Tarver is a lowly Major that didn't come from a whole lot. They didn't really like each other at first either, but what are you going to do when your trapped in a pod with someone trying to escape the destruction of the ship you were on? The Icarus was being ripped from space and Lilac and Tarver need to get that pod out quickly. <br><br>They managed to get away with the help of some mechanics from Lilac, I know, who knew? Anyway, they crash land on this planet. This planet that seems really creepy after a bit. I mean when you start seeing things and hearing whispers, wouldn't you think it was haunted? I would think I was crazier than I am or almost dead and dreaming. <br><br>Lilac and Tarver have to go through some really bad things and near death experiences to make it off this planet. They learned to survive in weird and cool ways. They fell in love, yes love and it was great! <br><br>But, things on this planet really are not what they seem. <br><br>I thought it was freaking awesome, even though I got lost with some of the explanations, but other than that it was cool beans! <br><br>I hope the other books are just as good!<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/04/these-broken-stars-by-amie-kaufman.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11971730494198412014"><strong>I probably read the wrong book.</strong><br/><br/><em>That cover…that blurb…that promising romance…</em><br/><br/><strong>A DNF. At 49%.</strong><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413000118ra/11454563.gif' width='500' height='220' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I wanted <em>so bad</em> to enjoy this in order to buy it in hardcover and have it in my library and admire it day and night. (Very slightly exaggerating.) The thing is, I am <strong>not one to buy books only for their beautiful cover</strong>. I have to like (of preference <em>love</em>) the actual story.<br/><br/>Except for the writing, nothing worked for me.<br/><br/>The pacing had such a slow speed that I just couldn’t continue. I always waiting for somethi</span>
  <span id="freeText11971730494198412014" style="display:none"><strong>I probably read the wrong book.</strong><br><br><em>That cover…that blurb…that promising romance…</em><br><br><strong>A DNF. At 49%.</strong><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413000118ra/11454563.gif" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wanted <em>so bad</em> to enjoy this in order to buy it in hardcover and have it in my library and admire it day and night. (Very slightly exaggerating.) The thing is, I am <strong>not one to buy books only for their beautiful cover</strong>. I have to like (of preference <em>love</em>) the actual story.<br><br>Except for the writing, nothing worked for me.<br><br>The pacing had such a slow speed that I just couldn’t continue. I always waiting for something interesting that would hook me to happen but nothing of such did. I expected an exciting survival story, romance apart, but, up to where I got, I didn’t even care if they died or not. Which makes me look very cold-hearted. I apologize but, still, that’s how I felt.<br><br>Because the main characters were awful. Lilac is unsupportable. I was sure I was going to appreciate her, because of how she doesn’t take ‘crap’ from anyone and knows what most guys want from her (because she's ''the daughter of the richest man in the universe'') and doesn’t let them get it. Turns out she’s annoying as hell and whiny and I couldn’t stand her.<br><br>Tarver started out being a likeable character, and I was sure I was going to<em> love</em> him. He’s honest and down-to-earth (but not too much) but also irritating and not always very nice. There were, in the story, this interview with Tarver cut in small bits that were inserted after some chapters. They were interesting at first but, then, Tarver really started getting on my nerves with his talking back and provoking replies.<br><br>The love/hate romance was so bad. There was mostly hate though.<br><blockquote>
  <strong>I’m positive he knows how much I hate it when he goes ahead to ‘‘scout.’’ He probably does it just to provoke me. I suppose he’s wandering off to imagine how much nicer it’d be not to have me around. Perhaps he’s even wishing he’d let that beast eat me yesterday.</strong>
</blockquote><br>Basically, he hates her.<br>But, also, she hates<em> him</em>.<br><br><strong>They really hate each other.</strong><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413000212i/11454570.jpg" width="500" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>JUST KISS ALREADY.</strong><br><br>Sigh, I definitely didn’t like this book. Though, I am in the minority so maybe you will.</span>

<div id="review_524448599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/524448599" />
    <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit"><img alt="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372018610p2/3854740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/524448599?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (Ensconced in Lit)" href="/user/show/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit">Christina (Ensconced in Lit)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3854740-christina-ensconced-in-lit?shelf=won">won</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer524448599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1664127136794904191">I won a copy of this ARC from Disney Publishers, and I haven't gotten a chance to read it until now. What a mistake. This is by far my favorite YA read from 2013.<br/><br/>These Broken Stars, written by the duo Amie Kaufman and Meagan Spooner, takes us to space aboard a massive luxury ship, similar to the Titanic. We immediately meet our two main characters-- Tarver, a solider, and Lilac, the daughter of the richest and most powerful man in the universe. Right away, something happens to the ship, and the </span>
  <span id="freeText1664127136794904191" style="display:none">I won a copy of this ARC from Disney Publishers, and I haven't gotten a chance to read it until now. What a mistake. This is by far my favorite YA read from 2013.<br /><br />These Broken Stars, written by the duo Amie Kaufman and Meagan Spooner, takes us to space aboard a massive luxury ship, similar to the Titanic. We immediately meet our two main characters-- Tarver, a solider, and Lilac, the daughter of the richest and most powerful man in the universe. Right away, something happens to the ship, and the two of them are stranded on a deserted planet left to forage and survive on their own without help. Slowly, something happens between them, beautiful and fragile. And in the end, Tarver and Lilac will have to make the difficult decision of giving up the wonderful peace they've found with each other to find their way back to civilization.<br /><br />Any plot synopsis won't do this book justice. The way Lilac and Tarver interact is perfect. The prose is gorgeous. The world building is immense and believable. And I even went along with the science, because it's clear that these two authors have done their homework. Just fantastic. I can go on and on about the lush description, the pitch perfect characterization, and the most successfully done dual POV I have seen maybe ever in YA. I actually wonder if each voice was written by a different author, because the two voices are very unique, and I never wondered whose perspective I was in. Each scene is deliberate, ramping up the tension and the stakes, and ultimately, having us care about these two characters so much that one heart wrenching plot twist is entirely a shock to the system. I had to sit stunned for a day before I could continue, and then devoured the pages until the end to see what happened.<br /><br />Overall, this book is a gem. I can't think of a single criticism, and my inner writer is salivating with jealousy. I can't say enough how people must read this book immediately. It's beautifully written, described, and characterized with perfect pacing. My favorite YA read of the past year, and I'll be waiting impatiently until I can get my hands on the next installment.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1664127136794904191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8416770787861890906" style="display:none">** Look for my tour stop (hosted by <a href="http://themidnightgarden.net" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Midnight Garden</a>) <a href="http://booksandwhimsy.com" rel="nofollow noopener"> on the blog</a> on 11/25/13 and a chance to enter an awesome THESE BROKEN STARS giveaway! **<br><br>5 stars simply isn't enough. Terrific world-building, heart-stopping action, poignant romance, and two of the best written characters I've ever come across. <br><br>OR IN GIFS TO EXPRESS MY FEEEEEEEELS:<br><br>THESE BROKEN STARS = TITANIC in space. Thus, Tarver = Jack Dawson, and Lilac = Rose. <br><br>Let's meet Lilac, aboard the Icarus:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688623.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This is Lilac at the beginning of THESE BROKEN STARS. A society girl who has problems, problems that authors Kaufman and Spooner actually manage to make resonate with me. (It should be noted I am not a rich person, nor do I typically feel for rich people in books. In this one? I did.) Despite finding Lilac infuriating, I eventually came to like her. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688624.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, meet Tarver: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688625.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked Tarver immediately. I <b>LOVED</b> Tarver immediately. I couldn't help but think of the scene in Titanic where Jack is <s>set up</s> invited to dinner by Cal, and ends up schooling everyone there. Tarver doesn't really belong in society, but he's sort of a quiet bad-ass, and I adored him. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688626.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Tarver + Lilac grabbed my attention. Tarver has no idea who Lilac is at first, but he's drawn to her. And *I* was drawn to *them.* <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688627.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though at first it was less swoon-y and more like this: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688628.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But EVENTUALLY their prejudices toward one another melted away as they were forced to work together. They started to really see each other for who they were. Things happen - dangerous, mysterious things. Tarver and Lilac begin to change, to become better versions of themselves. <br><br>And even though there are so MANY themes to this novel: a crash-landing reveals Tarver and Lilac's hearts, there's a not-so-barren planet to cross, mysteries to investigate, and their very survival to fight for... <br><br>The romance got under my skin and made me swoon. Their clashes of will were so powerful. It was SO CLEAR these two were feeling something for one another, and yet just as evident that their stations in life, and their fighting for survival threatened to keep them apart. But I LOVED seeing their attitudes change, seeing them become allies, with the potential for more. <br><br>Oh, and then this happened, basically: <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688629.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688630.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688631.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688632.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688633.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380312247ra/688634.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Want to know more about THESE BROKEN STARS? Want to know if Tarver and Lilac ever get together? What's going on on this planet? Why I feel like the authors may be fans of Doctor Who? If they make it to the crash site, or beyond? IF THERE IS KISSING?<br><br>Read THESE BROKEN STARS.<br><br>You're welcome. <br><br>Full review will appear at Books and Whimsy in December. A slightly different/longer GIF review is <a href="http://booksandwhimsy.com/warm-up-review-these-broken-stars-by-amie-kaufman-and-megan-spooner/" rel="nofollow noopener"> here</a>.<br><br>You can read my full review of THESE BROKEN STARS at <a href="http://booksandwhimsy.com/review-these-broken-stars-by-amie-kaufman-and-megan-spooner/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Books and Whimsy!</a></span>

<div id="review_836460233" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/836460233" />
    <a title="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5606933-that-s-all-ash"><img alt="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391795207p2/5606933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/836460233?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash" href="/user/show/5606933-that-s-all-ash">&quot;That&#39;s All&quot; Ash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5606933-that-s-all-ash?shelf=ehh">ehh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer836460233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7466964043335403756">Good job, Disney!<br/><br/>4-star book.<br/><br/>2-star ending.<br/><br/><b>Kind of like Miley Cyrus.</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_inline_mvgcy21D5U1s294hr.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391373315ra/8378843.gif' alt=' photo tumblr_inline_mvgcy21D5U1s294hr.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>:)<br/><br/>It’s a futuristic sci/fi fantasy book. And the <b>rudiment</b> of the story is that the richest girl in the galaxy gets stranded on a planet with a military boy. So, we’ve all read this story before, right? It’s one that has been done over and <b>over</b> and over again. But the thing with <i>These Broken Stars</i> is that there’s actually <b>a lot</b> of originality in this book! It’s co-written by two brilliant ladies, Amie Kaufman and Meagan Spoo</span>
  <span id="freeText7466964043335403756" style="display:none">Good job, Disney!<br><br>4-star book.<br><br>2-star ending.<br><br><b>Kind of like Miley Cyrus.</b> <br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_inline_mvgcy21D5U1s294hr.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391373315ra/8378843.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_mvgcy21D5U1s294hr.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>:)<br><br>It’s a futuristic sci/fi fantasy book. And the <b>rudiment</b> of the story is that the richest girl in the galaxy gets stranded on a planet with a military boy. So, we’ve all read this story before, right? It’s one that has been done over and <b>over</b> and over again. But the thing with <i>These Broken Stars</i> is that there’s actually <b>a lot</b> of originality in this book! It’s co-written by two brilliant ladies, Amie Kaufman and Meagan Spooner. I thought the writing was fucking <b>fabulous</b>, and I thought the little dialogue sequences they wrote in between chapters was very creative and witty. <br><br>I <b>loved</b> the first 65% percent or so. There was a little romance, a little camaraderie, a little bit of a creepiness factor, and whole <b>lot</b> of survival! What really kept me turning the pages though, definitely would have to be that creepiness factor. See, Lilac (the rich heroine) and Tarver (the military boy) are the only living people on this planet. There are animals and trees and everything <i>else</i> but they never come across people. <br><br>But Lilac’s hearing whispers.<br>Items keep turning up, out of nowhere. <br>She’s seeing things that haven’t quite happened yet. <br>And she thinks she’s going mad, which Tarver silently agrees with.<br><br><b>Until he starts hallucinating, too.</b><br><br>They’re being followed, haunted, and hunted.<br><br><b>But by what…?</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <u>SHAME ON YOU FOR CLICKING ON THIS! ;) </u>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So the formula of this story was very entertaining. However, the <b>ending</b> completely killed off any potential that this book had of being considered a 4-star book.<br><br><b>Here’s why:</b><br><br>The ending just had <i>waaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaaay</i> too much going on! Holy hot taffy on a cheese stick, man! It’s one thing to toss in a lot of action at the end of a book, but it’s a <b>whole</b> different thing when you try to beat your readers over the head with it. Know what I mean?<br><br><b>Me at 75%:</b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_inline_mvappw6nyx1s294hr.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391373315ra/8378844.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_mvappw6nyx1s294hr.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Yep.<br><br>I mean, what with the <i>terraforming</i> and the <i>hyperspace theries</i> and the <i>hyperspace rifts</i> and the <i>energy lifeforms</i>…<br><br><u>And I’m like:</u><br><br><b>Look, I got a A- minus in Biology and a C+ in Physics when I couldn’t manage to cheat off the mathlete sitting in front of me. And in my head, the hyperspace rift looks a lot like a Snickers bar wrapper. <br><br>*Which I <i>know</i> can’t be accurate.*<br><br>So can we just slow it down? Pretty please? </b><br><br>Also…<br><br>I don’t know if YA writers go to a seminar on writing sex scenes, but why is it that almost <i>every</i> YA book writes a sex scene a lot like this:<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Chapter 27:</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>They kissed. And then they woke up in post-coital bliss.</i><br><br><u>
  <i>
    <b> . . .Chapter 28.</b>
  </i>
</u><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_msmi4xXLfM1swmz50o3_500.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391373315ra/8378845.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_msmi4xXLfM1swmz50o3_500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I mean, come ON!<br><br>Anyway…<br><br><u>Do I recommend this book?</u><br>Sure.<br><br><u>Who do I recommend it to?</u><br>YA lovers and those who like socks.<br><br><u>One word to describe this book?</u><br>Unpredictable.<br><br><u>What book would I compare this to?</u><br><i>Cinder</i> by Marissa Mayer (only without the good romance).<br><br><b>That’s all.</b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_mks2m9FUgO1rknrf9o1_500.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1391373315ra/8378846.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mks2m9FUgO1rknrf9o1_500.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_630794475" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630794475" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/630794475?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer630794475" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9178889147213790019">This book reminds me why I love reading so much. <br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/amie-kaufman/review-these-broken-stars.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445267406i/16623040.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>...How trilling it is to dive into a new story, a new world, new lives and new adventures that leave me breathless every time!<br/><br/>This was such an unusual & original story! I have nothing to measure it against. It was nothing like I thought it would be. The world building is awesome, the action is trilling, the characters are strong and determined, the turnarounds made me tear a bit and the ending left me full of hope. <br/><br/>THESE BROKEN STARS tells a s</span>
  <span id="freeText9178889147213790019" style="display:none">This book reminds me why I love reading so much. <br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/amie-kaufman/review-these-broken-stars.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445267406i/16623040.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>...How trilling it is to dive into a new story, a new world, new lives and new adventures that leave me breathless every time!<br><br>This was such an unusual &amp; original story! I have nothing to measure it against. It was nothing like I thought it would be. The world building is awesome, the action is trilling, the characters are strong and determined, the turnarounds made me tear a bit and the ending left me full of hope. <br><br>THESE BROKEN STARS tells a story about survival, about love, about deadly secrets and hope that can make a heart beat again. I fell for this book from the beginning and, as the story progressed, I simply couldn’t stop reading.<br><br>To put it simple, we have our sweet couple (the rich girl and the famous -but poor- soldier) thrown into an unknown &amp; mostly unwelcome world, surviving a deadly accident (that might or might not have left other survivors) and being forced to cooperate in order to keep alive, which turns out to be hard when they each of them is as stubborn as a mule.<br>... But to be honest, this story is anything but ‘simple’.<br><br>So, we find a bit about the society in which our characters live, with the ups and downs on both sides. We find about their fears and hopes. We find about the mysteries of this new planet. We watch our characters struggle to move on and find a way back home. And yes, slowly they start to also fall in love, and it’s a bitter-sweet story because there is a lot of pride in the middle and some secrets to fear of. Not to mention that there’s a world of a problem that could tear them apart.<br><br>Still, what I really loved in this book is watching these broken characters start healing through what they’re forced to survive together – they grow stronger, more defined with each page and they start to see this world and the freedom it offers with different eyes.<br><br>I am glad that the next book won’t be about the same couple (or so I heard) as they’ve been through too much, through hell and back and I want to keep hoping.<br><br>Well, I am no fool here, I know that this will not be the end of their story, someone that has built such an empire won’t so easily be set off track, not with the secrets Lilac and Tarver share, not with the truth about her. But I’d like to be left guessing, I love this feeling of closure &amp; hope and I am gonna stick with it for as long as I can.<br><br>Conclusion:<br>From the fabulous cover, the magical world and the beautiful characters to the terrible turnarounds and fantastic plot, this story is absolutely great. My kind of book. No... <i>my kind of favourite book</i> and I recommend it from the bottom of my heart!<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/amie-kaufman/review-these-broken-stars.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_633990722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/633990722" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/633990722?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer633990722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer75090952302322510">Guys! This is not a story about a girl flying in space in a dress! That's only in the first chapter. I swear!<br/><br/>Actually, most of this book is a survival story. After a crash land on an anonymous planet, Tarver and Lilac have to find a way to get along and stay alive amongst the wild animals and Lilac's questionable state of mind. It's not a fast paced read, but rather a slow trek on this mysterious planet full of whispers, visions, ghosts, and other bizarre happenings. This is what keeps it comple</span>
  <span id="freeText75090952302322510" style="display:none">Guys! This is not a story about a girl flying in space in a dress! That's only in the first chapter. I swear!<br><br>Actually, most of this book is a survival story. After a crash land on an anonymous planet, Tarver and Lilac have to find a way to get along and stay alive amongst the wild animals and Lilac's questionable state of mind. It's not a fast paced read, but rather a slow trek on this mysterious planet full of whispers, visions, ghosts, and other bizarre happenings. This is what keeps it completely enthralling. You get that constant need to read just one more chapter to try and get some answers as to what exactly is happening in this weird place. Is Lilac going insane, or are the voices real? <br><br>Told in dual point-of-views, we get the story from polar opposite perspectives. Tarver is on his turf. He was trained to survive in situations like these. He's an award winning leader and expert in motivating people, pushing them to do what is needed to survive. I really enjoyed his strength, his drive, and especially his patience with Lila who, on a completely different standpoint has never been close to being in a situation like this where a ball gown is impractical and things are…. dirty. The character growth that Lila goes through during this ordeal is impressive, and frankly I was so thankful for it. I could have slapped her at the beginning, but she really changes completely until I came to fully adore her. As expected, there's a romance that sprouts between these two. It's sweet and genuine, bringing out an emotional side to the story that becomes fairly monumental when certain unexpected turn of events are strung out at us. I really really wish I could talk about these! *forcefully keeps her mouth shut*<br><br>In addition to the dual POV we also get interview sessions between each chapter. These are very brief but full of hidden meaning. I both loved and hated them, however. I disliked them because it tells us from the start that they were rescued and are now being questioned about what happened on the planet. This makes the anxiety in regards to them surviving a little less so. On the other hand, they deepen the mystery just a smudge more when we see Tarver being so strongly interrogated. You just know what they saw on that planet - what we're about to find out - is worth this much scrutiny. In regards to the plot, I can't say much obviously, but it becomes fairly mind-boggling as far as the sci-fi aspect. Some of it I'm still putting together, but overall I was quite impressed with the originality and imaginative nature of it all. Still, this sci-fi conspiracy side of the book was not my favorite - for personal taste more than anything. The main reason I loved it is due to the character oriented, suspense-filled survival story that encompasses 90% of it. Therefore, I'm not sure what I will make of the series as a whole (edit: apparently the others are companions so I'm excited!), but as far as this first installment I couldn't get enough!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380236618i/681468.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="75090952302322510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1031931740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1031931740" />
    <a title="Vanessa J." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j"><img alt="Vanessa J." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468102148p2/19590155.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1031931740?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=love-the-cover">love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1031931740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12633162038961500335"><b>DNF at 51%</b><br/><br/>God, I can't do this to myself. I kept telling myself I must have been reading the wrong book, because EVERYONE loved this, but... I just can't see why.<br/><br/>Many reviewers have described this as Titanic in space, and that is a great description. Thing is, this is a love story. That's all. The first time Tarver sees Lilac, he thinks she's the most beautiful girl there, and it only gets more cheesy and cliched the more I read. Ugh.<br/><br/>When I got to the 50% mark I stopped and asked myself: Why am </span>
  <span id="freeText12633162038961500335" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 51%</b><br /><br />God, I can't do this to myself. I kept telling myself I must have been reading the wrong book, because EVERYONE loved this, but... I just can't see why.<br /><br />Many reviewers have described this as Titanic in space, and that is a great description. Thing is, this is a love story. That's all. The first time Tarver sees Lilac, he thinks she's the most beautiful girl there, and it only gets more cheesy and cliched the more I read. Ugh.<br /><br />When I got to the 50% mark I stopped and asked myself: Why am I continuing with this anyway? My brain's answer was silence, and that's when I realised I should stop torturing myself with a book that was giving me headaches.<br /><br />You see, we are promised an epic journey through space, and that's why I started it. If you didn't know, getting lost in space (or the fact of getting out of Earth) is one of my biggest fears. Think about it: You're getting lost in something that may be <i>infinite</i>. God, no, it's horrible. I wanted to see how this book would manage that situation, but that's not what we got. A summary of what happened up until where I abandoned this was:<br /><br /><i>Tarver: *sees Lilac* OMG, isn't she <i>so pretty</i>?<br />Lilac: *sees Tarver* I will let him flirt with me for a while.<br /><br />*spaceship crashes*<br /><br />T: Oh, no, my lovebird is in danger! I must risk my life to save her!<br /><br />*L &amp; T land safely on a weird planet*<br /><br />T: Well, we made it. Now, are your shoes okay?<br />L: *looks the <b>high heels</b> she's wearing* Yes.<br />T: Don't you want to get rid off them? I mean, we are on a desert planet and we know absolutely nothing about it. We might have to run at some point.<br />L: Nah.<br /><br />*there's danger and they have to run*<br /><br />L: Shit, you were right. You can take off my shoes and bandage my feet.<br /><br />*T does that*<br /><br />T: Isn't this place cold?<br />L: Yeah.<br />T: We must give each other heat. Let me wrap my arms around you.<br />L: Okay.</i><br /><br />That's pretty much everything. Really, where is the survival story? Where is the thrill and terror of being alone is space? But above all, where is the epic sci-fi story I was promised?!?! I don't know and I don't care enough to keep reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12633162038961500335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
