<div id="review_639448161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/639448161" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/639448161?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=aussie-authors">aussie-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2013">best-of-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer639448161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16411798110038700221">Oh. Wow. Just OH WOW. (I swear this review will be a little more coherent. Honest.) This book was TOP of my want-right-now list, because of a) the beautiful cover, and b) YA sci-fi. It did not disappoint. Not even a little bit! It’s so freakishly amazing I want to recommend it to every human, alien, and stray cat. GO READ IT! <br/><br/>Where do I start? I could just say “the entire book from cover to cover is amazing”, but that’s not a helpful review, is it? I shall explain the awesomeness. No. Too much. </span>
  <span id="freeText16411798110038700221" style="display:none">Oh. Wow. Just OH WOW. (I swear this review will be a little more coherent. Honest.) This book was TOP of my want-right-now list, because of a) the beautiful cover, and b) YA sci-fi. It did not disappoint. Not even a little bit! It’s so freakishly amazing I want to recommend it to every human, alien, and stray cat. GO READ IT! <br /><br />Where do I start? I could just say “the entire book from cover to cover is amazing”, but that’s not a helpful review, is it? I shall explain the awesomeness. No. Too much. I shall sum up.<br /><br />Premise? It’s a sci-fi! Of course the premise is awesome. I love the huge space-ships doing warp speed with all their laser guns and stuff. What I DID NOT know though, was that this is a survival book. I don’t know why this isn’t promoted more! That’s awesome. I’ve always loved books like HATCHET by Gary Paulson. And surviving a deserted planet with deathly secrets? Yes, please. <br /><br />Characters? I adore them. Lilac LaRoux is a “princess”. Not literally, though she might as well be. She’s a stuck-up snob, but not because she wants to be. She does it to protect people. Her father basically controls the galaxy (he’s the stinking rich kind) and he dotes on her. Usually snobs are hard to like at the beginning of books. Not Lilac. Her voice was spot-on. I loved her from the start and never once thought her too complainy or whiny. She was the best. She dual narrates with Tarver.<br /><br />Where do I begin with Tarver? He’s every bit the epic, young, war-hero, gentlemen. Except that he’s feisty. His humour was awesome! I loved how he was frustrated out of his brain cells because of Lilac, but he was never cruel to her. I love how he kept being a gentleman – no matter what the circumstances, his feelings, his thoughts. Since it’s duel narrated, I was worried their voices would be easy to confuse. No way. They were so different and so alive!<br /><br />What I loved most about Tarver and Lilac is – they hated each other! It’s hilarious. Of course, they don’t stay that way (it is kind of a romance after all), but they’re so snarky at the beginning. They’re so 3-dimensional. <br /><br />Between each chapter is a snippet of Tarver being interrogated. You don’t know when it is or why or who’s asking the questions. (It’s like the snippets at the beginning of each chapter in ENDER’S GAME.) I loved these! My only criticism is: some of them sounded the same. I couldn’t decided if they were the best part of the book, or too repetitive. <br /><br />It’s a big book, but the plot is interesting 99% of the time. I leave off the 1% only because sometimes I felt the chapters will killing time. The same stuff happened. Walk. Sleep. Hate each other. So what? Don’t get me wrong, I adoooored all of that, but I just wish it varied more. <br /><br />The ending will blow your mind. I don’t say that lightly either! I can’t – I still don’t – woah. <br /><br />This goes down as one of my best-reads-of-2013. Easily. It’s a sci-fi that’s worth every centimetre of its huge hype. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16411798110038700221" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2349622283" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2349622283" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2349622283?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=apocalyptic-post-apocalytic">apocalyptic-post-apocalytic</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2349622283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8138264185436565902">What started out a space opera ended up in a story of survival out in the wilderness of a strange, abandoned planet and once again, it surprises me how much I enjoyed the book from start to end. In some instances, the reading experience reminded me a little of that when I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23395680.Illuminae__The_Illuminae_Files___1_' title='Illuminae (The Illuminae Files, #1) by Amie Kaufman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Illuminae</a> especially in the last quarter of the story when the plot reveals the ultimate twist explainable by scientific stuff like hyperspace, other dimensions and temporary energy-matter conversion. I won’t pretend to un</span>
  <span id="freeText8138264185436565902" style="display:none">What started out a space opera ended up in a story of survival out in the wilderness of a strange, abandoned planet and once again, it surprises me how much I enjoyed the book from start to end. In some instances, the reading experience reminded me a little of that when I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23395680.Illuminae__The_Illuminae_Files___1_" title="Illuminae (The Illuminae Files, #1) by Amie Kaufman" rel="nofollow noopener">Illuminae</a> especially in the last quarter of the story when the plot reveals the ultimate twist explainable by scientific stuff like hyperspace, other dimensions and temporary energy-matter conversion. I won’t pretend to understand all of it but I grasped enough to appreciate the general idea. <br /><br />What I enjoyed most about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13138635.These_Broken_Stars__Starbound___1_" title="These Broken Stars (Starbound, #1) by Amie Kaufman" rel="nofollow noopener">These Broken Stars</a> though aside from the simple but beautiful and fluid writing is the progressive character development of our hero and heroine, <b>Tarver and Lilac.</b>. How they do their best to survive in a strange planet that whispers to them and gives them visions is very admirable and I find them both growing on me each day they struggle hanging on dear life. Of course, I’ve been rooting for their romance since the start of the book but how theirs developed is even better and more adorable than I expected.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_541545763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/541545763" />
    <a title="Mara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10194700-mara"><img alt="Mara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599132109p2/10194700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/541545763?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mara" href="/user/show/10194700-mara">Mara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10194700-mara?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10194700-mara?shelf=rereads">rereads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer541545763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15664576341494163810">This book though. These Broken Stars was most definitely my most anticipated release of 2013, with that cover luring me in like sirens do sailors at sea ever since its release announcement. I mean, that cover is probably the most beautiful thing I had seen all year. It has the perfect space odyssey/mythology ratio that just did it for me even way before I knew what the whole story was about. I was so, so happy when These Broken Stars became everything I had hoped for. I finished it in three hour</span>
  <span id="freeText15664576341494163810" style="display:none">This book though. These Broken Stars was most definitely my most anticipated release of 2013, with that cover luring me in like sirens do sailors at sea ever since its release announcement. I mean, that cover is probably the most beautiful thing I had seen all year. It has the perfect space odyssey/mythology ratio that just did it for me even way before I knew what the whole story was about. I was so, so happy when These Broken Stars became everything I had hoped for. I finished it in three hours without a single break because, yup, it was that good.<br /><br />These Broken Stars has been helmed as ‘Titanic in space’ so often I couldn’t pass a chance to mention it. It’s a perfect tagline, really, for a story about two star-crossed lovers who travel through space on one of the most advanced ships ever built. Here’s the thing, though, where These Broken Stars manages to make a name of it’s very own – we leave behind the Titanic disaster element of the story fairly early on, morphing into a haunting survival story that reveals evermore injustices of this sci-fi dystopian universe. After the Icarus crashes on an unknown planet, the two leads are faced with an unexplored terrain, an eerie presence that radiates through the lands, and whether or not they have the will and reason to make it out of this tragedy alive.<br /><br />The book’s opening chapters are incredibly spot-on. We meet both main characters, Lilac LaRoux – daughter to the richest man in the galaxy – and Tarver Merendsen – the youngest war hero of said galaxy – right in the beginning. We immediately know they’re going to be in each other’s lives for far longer than initially set up as, and yet you keep wondering that maybe their stories aren’t going to intertwine for long at all. And that is what makes the crash and their subsequent journey together so much more compelling, because as much as we have learned about them as individuals, they have both so far acted out choices that would have had them not cross paths ever again. Most of the time, early meetings throw me off because I’d rather have a little bit of mystery within the plot, but both Lilac’s and Tarver’s inner monologues work their magic so convincingly, I didn’t mind once. There are doubts about their standpoints all the way through the story, and I think it takes a lot of skill to create characters that are both likable one instance and then dislikeable the next as they temporarily fall back into old patterns. It’s the easiest way to just go ahead and form perfect heroes and heroines out of words who do nothing wrong or who have a character development as fast as light travels, but Kaufman and Spooner have done a wonderful job to create real people instead of plot twist agents. Lilac and Tarver are both stubborn and condescending at times, and yet they are loyal, steadfast and compassionate, too. They both start off the journey with different morals and goals, yet manage to find a common ground throughout their track across the planet’s grass planes and rocky hills, and there’s just something about the connection they form that resonated deeply with me. They really just work so well together. The backdrop of the galaxy being but a small map due to the invention of hyperspace travel further made for such a unique mash with what Lilac and Tarver have to face at the end of the road, and that originality had me tear through the pages as fast as I could. The final 30% or so of the book had me gasping over every new chapter, there are so many bizarre things happening that made for a grandiose finale.<br /><br />The book’s structure is something that I feel needs a special mention, because every chapter has a 1-page-preface of sorts that consists of dialogue only from an interview being conducted with Tarver that took place at the end of the book. It created a heart-stopping suspense as well as some funny moments. I honestly can’t wait for the second book to arrive, even though that one will be about two new characters, but I’m 100% convinced it will be just as epic as this one. There’s a lot to tell about Kaufman and Spooner’s universe, and I can’t wait to see it unfold!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15664576341494163810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13442991792428398823"><b>SECOND ATTEMPT <br/>DNF @ 20%</b><br/><br/><b>BUDDY READING</b> with my wife, Caitlin. <br/><br/>I <i>tried</i>. Boy, did I try. I struggled through 20% of pointless interactions and pointless information to give up. This book just isn't for me and I'm sad because I really did want to like this. <br/><br/>In one of her updates Caitlin said this was basically the Titanic in space - I hate the Titanic. I hate the movie with a burning fiery passion of "wtf why did I just waste like two hours of my life??" <br/><br/>The characters are one dimensional for me. I </span>
  <span id="freeText13442991792428398823" style="display:none"><b>SECOND ATTEMPT <br />DNF @ 20%</b><br /><br /><b>BUDDY READING</b> with my wife, Caitlin. <br /><br />I <i>tried</i>. Boy, did I try. I struggled through 20% of pointless interactions and pointless information to give up. This book just isn't for me and I'm sad because I really did want to like this. <br /><br />In one of her updates Caitlin said this was basically the Titanic in space - I hate the Titanic. I hate the movie with a burning fiery passion of "wtf why did I just waste like two hours of my life??" <br /><br />The characters are one dimensional for me. I hate Lilac (I hate her name as well) and Tarver (is that his name? don't care). They're so annoying. The attempt at banter and snark is slightly painful to read. As are the descriptions and the slightly pervert moment Tarver has while Lilac is passed out. <br /><br />The insta-attraction still hurts me, as does Lilac's ridiculously immature reactions. It has so much potential, the execution is just poor for me. <br /><br /><b>FIRST ATTEMPT</b><br /><b>DNF @ 1%</b><br /><br />Now, I know what you're thinking: <br /><br /><i>Amber, you've only read one percent?!</i><br /><br />So stay with me kids, because I have the perfect reason for not continuing on. <b>Insta-attraction.</b> Oh, and cliches as hell. <br /><br /><i>Insta-attraction?!</i><br /><br />I use this because it wasn't love, but the descriptions used for the girl I presume to be the female lead where of such an insta-love way I was rolling around on my bed cringing. <br /><br /><i>Shouldn't you at least give the book a chance?</i><br /><br />No. I'm not wasting my time with crappy books anymore. They're not worth the energy and reading slumps that follow. I am, however, really upset I didn't enjoy this.</span>

<div id="review_1119673769" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1119673769" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1119673769?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1119673769" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6316734962530652393"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“But who names a starship the Icarus? What kind of man possess that much hubris, that he dares it to fall?” </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441629015i/16131126.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I went into These Broken Stars expecting a Titanic retelling. We all remember what happens at the end; Kate is a dumbass and runs after Jack, then they both get stranded and Jack freezes to death. Also, he never wins an Oscar.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441629015ra/16131127.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But I digress. My point is, a Titanic retelling has to have at least two things: a sink sinks, and someone dies. <br/><br/>And guess what? <b>No one dies.</b> <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoil</a></span>
  <span id="freeText6316734962530652393" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“But who names a starship the Icarus? What kind of man possess that much hubris, that he dares it to fall?” </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441629015i/16131126.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I went into These Broken Stars expecting a Titanic retelling. We all remember what happens at the end; Kate is a dumbass and runs after Jack, then they both get stranded and Jack freezes to death. Also, he never wins an Oscar.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441629015ra/16131127.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But I digress. My point is, a Titanic retelling has to have at least two things: a sink sinks, and someone dies. <br><br>And guess what? <b>No one dies.</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>I was in awe of the writers' balls when they killed Lilac, then brought her back to life as a ghost-like figure. There are so many things you can play with. So many moral grey areas you can touch upon. What makes a person a person? Ghost Lilac remember everything the old Lilac did, is solid and has a heartbeat. But her clothes are conjured from nothing, the real Lilac's rags left behind long ago, and real Lilac's corpse is still rotting in the ground. <br><br>What complexity. What ingenuity. What <i>guts</i>.<br><br>But then she comes back to life through a blast of supernatural energy. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441629015ra/16131128.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know what I call that? Deux ex-fucking-machina. The writers didn't have the balls to let her be dead. <br><br>The ending is tied up in a neat little bow. Lilac's daddy, who once sent a boy to the front lines of a battle for having the gall to date her, lets her have her way because of a little back-sass. Their social differences are swept aside and no one gives a damn the richest heiress in the galaxy is dating a guy from the back alleys. Whoopdee-freaking-do. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's cowardly and ruined the entire book for me.<br><br>Everything else I loved. The writing's strong and descriptive without getting too purple. I would compare it to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4342215.Marie_Lu" title="Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Marie Lu</a>'s style.<br><br>The characters remind me of Day and June from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9275658.Legend__Legend___1_" title="Legend (Legend, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Legend</a>, too. Lilac LaRoux is the daughter of the most powerful man in the galaxy, the creator and owner of LaRoux Industries. She was born with a silver spoon in her mouth and has never had to work a single day in her life.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"There are jokes about how the LaRoux princess never goes anywhere without her entourage of giggling companions--that half of them could kill a man at a hundred yards is not exactly public knowledge. The President's family doesn't have protection like mine." </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Then there's Tarver. The war hero from humble beginnings.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"These folks love a good rags-to-riches tale, even if my riches are no more than the medals pinned to my chest."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>After the Icarus is blasted out of hyperspace, they crash-land on a foreign planet with no way of communicating with the outside world. They're forced to work together to survive, though initially it's mostly Tarver that does the working. Lilac's journey looks something like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441630345ra/16131285.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know I'm making her sound like Paris Hilton, but she's really not. She can hold her own. She's a kickass mechanic and learns to adapt after a rough start. <br><br>Tarver sounds like an actual teenage boy, which is rare in YA, so good job there. I'm struggling for what else to say about him, but keep coming up short. He's nice, he's competent, but I wouldn't put him on my Book Boyfriend List, let's leave it at that.<br><br>A good, solid book overall. I just wish the authors had more guts.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6316734962530652393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1226585255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1226585255" />
    <a title="Mandy K" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2990684-mandy-k"><img alt="Mandy K" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1561995080p2/2990684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1226585255?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mandy K" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mandy K" href="/user/show/2990684-mandy-k">Mandy K</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2990684-mandy-k?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2990684-mandy-k?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1226585255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3842901960990210874"><a href='http://ohdangmandy.blogspot.com/2015/04/review-these-broken-stars-by-amie.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Full Review</a><br/><br/>Part <i>Titanic</i> in space, part <i>I Shouldn't Be Alive</i> and part <i>Doctor Who/The Twilight Zone</i>, this is a sci-fi/fantasy/survivor story/romance all in one and I loved it! We start out on the glamourous <i>Icarus</i>, and have just enough time to get a taste for the gigantic luxury spaceliner when she is yanked from hyberspace and sucked into an unknown planets gravity. Our main characters Lilac LaRoux and Tarver Merenderson end up in a crew escape pod and just barely survive the crash down to the pl</span>
  <span id="freeText3842901960990210874" style="display:none"><a href="http://ohdangmandy.blogspot.com/2015/04/review-these-broken-stars-by-amie.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Full Review</a><br /><br />Part <i>Titanic</i> in space, part <i>I Shouldn't Be Alive</i> and part <i>Doctor Who/The Twilight Zone</i>, this is a sci-fi/fantasy/survivor story/romance all in one and I loved it! We start out on the glamourous <i>Icarus</i>, and have just enough time to get a taste for the gigantic luxury spaceliner when she is yanked from hyberspace and sucked into an unknown planets gravity. Our main characters Lilac LaRoux and Tarver Merenderson end up in a crew escape pod and just barely survive the crash down to the planet. Although the planet is terraformed, its quickly apart that something isn't right here. The flora and fauna are more wild and uncontained than they should be, and there doesn't seem to be any civilization on the planet.<br /><br />I love a good survival story, and that comes in handy because a big chunk of this book is Lilac and Tarver trekking across the land, trying to survive and get rescued. But we also have mystery woven through out. Where are all the people? Why does Traver not recognize the plants and animals here? Why would anyone spend all this money to terraform a planet, and then seemingly abandon it? <br /><br />And then the whispers start and theres even more questions. What are the whispers? Are they real? What do they want?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3842901960990210874" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UAKWLV92vJHwalbFfXgaHy5kMtTGWGCgjBWfRtPh5K1t8/FhkFUaH4quVNZg68JgchUwbbtPlhex2t1pjPpQcw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ybc47YQUnYUsMkkvGoHTrL802GLIxdEoJMJjMAFZjOX0Rl+hSzc7C1b2SzwHEgvT40Xa27XSJ58ZDSEfXkI4Ow==')})
  }
//]]>

<span id="freeTextContainer9884941680306827589">Amie Kaufman is a New York Times and internationally bestselling author of young adult fiction. Her multi-award winning work is slated for publication in over 30 countries, and is in development for film and TV. Raised in Australia and occasionally Ireland, Amie has degrees in history, literature, law and conflict resolution. She lives in Melbourne with her husband, their rescue dog, and an extrem</span>
  <span id="freeText9884941680306827589" style="display:none">Amie Kaufman is a New York Times and internationally bestselling author of young adult fiction. Her multi-award winning work is slated for publication in over 30 countries, and is in development for film and TV. Raised in Australia and occasionally Ireland, Amie has degrees in history, literature, law and conflict resolution. She lives in Melbourne with her husband, their rescue dog, and an extremely large personal library.<br /><br />You can sign up for her newsletter to see what she's working on, hear when she releases a new book, and be automatically entered for giveaways: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.eepurl.com/6Ya8j">www.eepurl.com/6Ya8j</a><br /></span>
